<div id="review_1827274756" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1827274756" />
    <a title="Stuart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9456990-stuart"><img alt="Stuart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452041473p2/9456990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1827274756?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stuart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stuart" href="/user/show/9456990-stuart">Stuart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=distant-worlds">distant-worlds</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=satirical-humorous">satirical-humorous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=hard-sf">hard-sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1827274756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18046687812788021949"><b>We Are Legion (We Are Bob): Geeky SF fun a la The Martian</b><br/>Originally posted <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/we-are-legion-we-are-bob/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a><br/>This seems to be a thing these days. Breezy, snarky SF stories by first-time authors that promote their own work, capture a lot of positive word-of-mouth and become very popular without major publisher help initially. I’m thinking of Andy Weir’s The Martian, Ernest Cline’s Ready Player One, and John Scalzi’s Old Man’s War. Basically, these books are a whole lot of fun, drop liberal 1980s geek references,</span>
  <span id="freeText18046687812788021949" style="display:none"><b>We Are Legion (We Are Bob): Geeky SF fun a la The Martian</b><br />Originally posted <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/we-are-legion-we-are-bob/" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a><br />This seems to be a thing these days. Breezy, snarky SF stories by first-time authors that promote their own work, capture a lot of positive word-of-mouth and become very popular without major publisher help initially. I’m thinking of Andy Weir’s The Martian, Ernest Cline’s Ready Player One, and John Scalzi’s Old Man’s War. Basically, these books are a whole lot of fun, drop liberal 1980s geek references, tell an exciting tale, and reject the dark and grim cyberpunk futures exemplified by William Gibson’s Neuromancer, Richard Morgan’s Altered Carbon, Alastair Reynolds’ Chasm City, etc. Don’t get me wrong, those are all excellent books too, but man, are they depressing! After listening to five Reynolds audiobooks in quick succession, I really needed something light and fun, and I happened to see Dennis E. Taylor’s We Are Legion (We Are Bob) (2016) mentioned as one of Audible’s Best SF of 2016, so on a lark I picked it up.<br /><br />It’s a very simple story. Bob Johansson is a young Internet entrepreneur who has just sold his successful business to a larger competitor. Flush with cash, he arranges for his body to be put in cryogenic storage when he dies as an insurance policy, and on the way to a SF convention he gets distracted crossing the street and…<br /><br />Wakes up 117 years later in a repressive future society that somewhat reminded me of Woody Allen’s classic SF spoof Sleeper (1973). We Are Legion (We Are Bob) is nothing if not topical — Taylor had me laughing out loud in painful acknowledgement with this succinct description of the future US theocracy. Obviously very different from our current world, thankfully…<br /><br /><i>In 2036, the USA elected an over-the-top, unapologetic fundamentalist president named Andrew Handel. Yes, that Handel. During his term, he tried to ban election of non-Christians to any public post, and tried to remove the constitutional separation between church and state. He was nominated, supported, and elected based on his religious views, rather than on his political or fiscal expertise. And of course, he appointed persons of similar persuasion to every post he could manage, in some cases blatantly ignoring laws and procedures. He and his cronies rammed through far-right policies with no thought for consequences. In a number of cases, when challenged on the results, he declared that God would not allow their just cause to fail. He eventually brought the USA to its knees in an economic collapse that made the 2008 recession look like a picnic in the park.</i><br /><br />Anyway, that is just laying the groundwork for the main part of the story, which is that Bob is now a bodiless AI, or replicant, that has been revived along with several other candidates for an urgent project by one faction of the current US government to seed the stars for humanity while competing with other rival nations. It turns out that most AIs turn insane when they understand their new situation, but Bob seems to have a better temperament for accepting his new existence as an AI that essentially controls a collection of servitors, etc. The choice is elegant — either accept the assignment to pilot a fleet of Von Neumann machines to seed new stars with colonies, or be shut off permanently.<br />Bob’s no-nonsense, self-deprecating internal monologue is the backbone of this enjoyable tale, very much like Mark Watney in The Martian. He always has a quip for each occasion, a super-rational and creative engineering mind, and indefatigable optimism no matter the circumstances. If you like that style of story, you’ll be in good hands, and the audiobook narration by Ray Porter is excellent. I found myself smiling at Bob’s one-liners and refusal to be dragged down by setbacks. He is a character any reader can root for.<br /><br />The bulk of the book involves Bob’s adventures escaping the ploys of other nation-states back on Earth, hostile rival AIs tasked with the same mission, and then the very existential struggle of Bob coming to terms with cloning himself into a multitude of Bobs, hence the book’s title We Are Legion (We Are Bob). Bob’s chats and debates with his other alter-egos are hilarious and probably the best part of the book. It also makes the book less claustrophobic than The Martian, because the other Bobs do have distinct character variations, essentially different aspects of the original Bob’s persona. They choose names for themselves like Riker, Homer, Garfield, etc., so we get plenty of 80s geek references just like Ready Player One.<br /><br />The final third of We Are Legion (We Are Bob) tells the adventures of Bob and his alter-egos as they encounter a more primitive species of humanoid aliens and play a bit of God trying to favor one group over another, much like a Star Trek scenario (you know, the Prime Directive and all that). The main mechanism that drives the engineering technology is the ability to use 3D printers to build anything with the right raw materials from asteroids and planets, so Bob has to decide between replicating himself, building colony ships for Earth’s survivors, and building other 3D printers. Imagine the SF version of “For my third wish I wish for unlimited wishes.” This is clearly intended as the opening salvo of an ongoing SF series, since Taylor can take Bob’s adventures in any direction he wants. If you are a fan of the books mentioned in this review, I think you’ll definitely enjoy the ride.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18046687812788021949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58882300-valliya-rennell?shelf=a-3-stars">a-3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58882300-valliya-rennell?shelf=x-reviewed-books">x-reviewed-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3252838075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16950503278831723843">3 stars<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32109569.We_Are_Legion__We_Are_Bob___Bobiverse___1_' title='We Are Legion (We Are Bob) (Bobiverse, #1) by Dennis E. Taylor' rel='nofollow noopener'>We Are Legion (We Are Bob)</a> is a novel that will definitely appeal to many sci-fi fans. There are so many <b>different story-lines: first contact, interplanetary war, human evacuation</b> etc. The premise is also very interesting. Just before he died Bob Johansson decided to sign up for a program where your brain gets cryogenically frozen in the hopes of being awakened many years later when technology is advanced enough that an organic body would be able to get crafted especially for you! Unfortu</span>
  <span id="freeText16950503278831723843" style="display:none">3 stars<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32109569.We_Are_Legion__We_Are_Bob___Bobiverse___1_" title="We Are Legion (We Are Bob) (Bobiverse, #1) by Dennis E. Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">We Are Legion (We Are Bob)</a> is a novel that will definitely appeal to many sci-fi fans. There are so many <b>different story-lines: first contact, interplanetary war, human evacuation</b> etc. The premise is also very interesting. Just before he died Bob Johansson decided to sign up for a program where your brain gets cryogenically frozen in the hopes of being awakened many years later when technology is advanced enough that an organic body would be able to get crafted especially for you! Unfortunately, things do not go as planned in history and the world gets divided up by new empires, countries, and theological associations. Now, <b>Bob's replica in the form of a computer is launched into space to help humanity expand. </b> As the reader you get to follow Bobs' adventures... because, yes, there is more than one Bob.<br /><br /><b>I really liked two story-lines and didn't really care for the others, but I think that they are still of value for many other sci-fi fans. </b>I loved the first contact story and enjoyed the human evacuation story. They were thought provoking and generally just really interesting to think about. The first contact story was OMG SO COOL! I loooved those chapters. It is hard to not go into spoilers, but if you are a fan of learning about new species and such, this will be just up your ally. One the other hand, the human evacuation story is interesting because of the comedic duo that Homer and Riker are (two Bob replicas). I enjoyed their banter and the way they strive to deal with the humans.<br /><br />The other stories I didn't really care for. As a person who never really felt strongly about Star Wars and Star Trek, I just didn't connect with these stories as much. <b>Fans of Star Wars and Star Trek will love the other stories, but they just weren't for me.</b> I think that this is the main reason that I just think of the book with neutral feelings as the homage paid to the two franchises really didn't have any meaning for me.<br /><br /><b>I loved the beginning and the world building. </b>Although it was quite info-dumpy at times, I overall really liked learning about how the world progressed into the theological dystopia that it is in the first 4-ish chapters.<br /><br />In the sequel, I am excited to follow my favorite story lines more as things are getting more and more exciting with the ending of the novel. I think that <b>many sci-fi fans will enjoy this much more than I did, so, especially if you watched Star Wars/Trek, read this book and you won't be disappointed.</b></span>

<div id="review_1989624411" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1989624411" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36819318-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485843897p2/36819318.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1989624411?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/36819318-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1989624411" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12425667997883756477">This book is <i>fun</i>. Fun, fun, fun. Genuine, enjoyable, page-turning fun of the sort that has you grinning while you read it.<br/><br/><i>We are Legion (We are Bob)</i> is that rare thing - a science fiction novel with both solid SF chops and a sense of humor. Imagine Andy Weir's <i>The Martian</i>, but swap the protagonist for Bob - a computer copy of a long-dead software engineer onboard an interstellar probe - and swap Mars for the entire galaxy as Bob travels into the cosmos making extra copies of himself enroute, fil</span>
  <span id="freeText12425667997883756477" style="display:none">This book is <i>fun</i>. Fun, fun, fun. Genuine, enjoyable, page-turning fun of the sort that has you grinning while you read it.<br /><br /><i>We are Legion (We are Bob)</i> is that rare thing - a science fiction novel with both solid SF chops and a sense of humor. Imagine Andy Weir's <i>The Martian</i>, but swap the protagonist for Bob - a computer copy of a long-dead software engineer onboard an interstellar probe - and swap Mars for the entire galaxy as Bob travels into the cosmos making extra copies of himself enroute, filling the universe with wisecracking, problem-solving pop-culture referencing Bob-clones. <br /><br />This is the first book in Dennis E. Taylor's 'Bobiverse' series and as the story begins Bob Johansson, a friendly thirty-one year old geek and software engineer, has just sold his company and become fabulously rich. Looking forward to a lifetime of doing as he pleases he visits a geek-con in Las Vegas, steps out on the street and gets fatally run down by a car.<br /><br />Luckily for Bob he used some of his buyout loot to engage a cryogenics company, and his head is whipped off and stored, awaiting a time in the future when he can be revived. Over a century later Bob reawakens, but he's not really Bob anymore. He's a copy of the original Bob, stored in a computer system, and he is owned by the corporation that bought his frozen head from the company storing it.<br /><br />Bob is soon told that he is being trained to control a Von Neumann probe- a self replicating interstellar ship that will replicate itself throughout the galaxy, searching for habitable worlds and sending info back to Earth.<br /><br />Bob is a little disconcerted by not having a body, and struggles with the revelation that he is a mere copy of the 'real' Bob, but the chance to explore the universe is something no true geek could turn down and he embraces his second life with gusto, learning to live with the limitations of being a piece of software.<br /><br />Earth is riven by struggles between competing power blocs with their own interstellar probe programs, and Bob has to deal with bombs, sabotage and political pressure before he even makes it into space. When he eventually reaches space, and begins to send copies of himself through the galaxy, <i>We are Legion</i> branches off into multiple engaging narratives across tens of light years. The device of having multiple slightly different versions of the same person is surprisingly effective. We get to follow along with uptight Bobs, gregarious Bobs, antisocial Bobs and of course, the original Bob as they explore strange new worlds, seek out new life etc. etc.(intentional Star Trek reference- the Bobs make a few of them in Taylor's book).<br /><br />Simply put, this is one of the best SF novels I've read this year (hell, in the past few years) and it's a welcome break from the heavier, grimmer stuff I usually gravitate to.<br /><br />Following the adventures of the multiplicity of curious, thoughtful Bobs is a reading experience I encourage you to have. The future of humanity can be threatened, Bobs can be dying in droves at the hands of enemy probes, and there will still be time for a sly joke, an amusing Sci-Fi reference, or a reflection on the nature of human (and post-human) life.<br /><br />Fun isn't a word I use to describe SF very often, but this novel was a genuinely enjoyable ride from the first page to the last. <i>We are Legion</i> combines a great concept with solid writing, interesting characters and a quirky sense of humor. <br /><br />I've already bought the sequel, and if you like SF I urge you to start your own trip through the Bobiverse.<br /><br />4.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12425667997883756477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2370315547" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2370315547" />
    <a title="Char " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6581119-char"><img alt="Char " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415394568p2/6581119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2370315547?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Char " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Char " href="/user/show/6581119-char">Char </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/32603222-we-are-legion-we-are-bob">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6581119-char?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2370315547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7077270199887688460">This book was totally out of my wheelhouse but I loved it!<br/><br/>Bob is a tech genius comparable to Bill Gates. He decides to get himself, (well, his head), cryogenically frozen and signs a contract to have it done. Shortly thereafter, he's hit by a car and the contract kicks in. <br/><br/>When he wakes up, it's centuries later and as a sentient computer. He's in charge of, (basically), saving humanity. He goes about this task by cloning himself, as he was made to do, (see Von Neumann probes), and spreading thro</span>
  <span id="freeText7077270199887688460" style="display:none">This book was totally out of my wheelhouse but I loved it!<br /><br />Bob is a tech genius comparable to Bill Gates. He decides to get himself, (well, his head), cryogenically frozen and signs a contract to have it done. Shortly thereafter, he's hit by a car and the contract kicks in. <br /><br />When he wakes up, it's centuries later and as a sentient computer. He's in charge of, (basically), saving humanity. He goes about this task by cloning himself, as he was made to do, (see Von Neumann probes), and spreading throughout the universe(s). He, (it), (Bobs), does this with humor, compassion and all kinds of science fiction references that cracked me up. <br /><br />A total aside: my husband was watching the Science Channel the other night and the show was talking about 3D printers and I asked if Von Neumann probes were mentioned. He looked at me as if I were a nut. No, he said. Two minutes later the show went into what they were and how they would work and I puffed up with pride. (Picture Fredo Corleone: "I'm smart!")<br /><br />Ray Porter is a fantastic narrator and I enjoyed hearing him voice the different faces of Bob: (Riker, Homer and Admiral Akbar), to name a few. I'm not sure I would have enjoyed this book as much if I had read it instead of listening. That said, bring on book two!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7077270199887688460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1808294374" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1808294374" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788446-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475256742p2/41788446.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1808294374?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/41788446-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/32603222-we-are-legion-we-are-bob">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788446-hannah?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788446-hannah?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1808294374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15806705597438274956">Sometimes I just want to read (or in this case listen) to something really fun. And this book delivered: so much fun! <br/><br/>This is Bob's story - Bob who has just sold his company for a ton of money and impulsively signs up to have his body frozen after death - and a good thing he did that, too, as he then meets his untimely demise - only to wake up way in the future where people who had their bodies frozen are not considered people anymore and thus have no rights. Bob then gets turned into an AI for </span>
  <span id="freeText15806705597438274956" style="display:none">Sometimes I just want to read (or in this case listen) to something really fun. And this book delivered: so much fun! <br /><br />This is Bob's story - Bob who has just sold his company for a ton of money and impulsively signs up to have his body frozen after death - and a good thing he did that, too, as he then meets his untimely demise - only to wake up way in the future where people who had their bodies frozen are not considered people anymore and thus have no rights. Bob then gets turned into an AI for an interstellar probe. I mean, come on, isn't this premise just the best? I am smiling just thinking about it. <br /><br />I really enjoyed the humour of this book before everything else - the jokes are well-timed and Bob's wry personality and his pop culture references really worked for me. The interactions between the different Bob's were bloody brilliant and reminded me of the way I am with my siblings. I loved the subtle (and not so subtle) differences between them and their names, oh, their names were marvelous.<br /><br />I like how this book is both pessimistic about the future (Faith? Scary, but believable. The New UN - annoyingly realistic in its bickering.) and optimistic about everything there is to discover (new planets! New species! Lots to see and invent!). <br /><br />I cannot wait to listen to the next book in this series!<br />...I should stop starting series that aren't finished yet though...</span>
  <a data-text-id="15806705597438274956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('D0bkAeOd2HCg/DMiPZVn3flUXVHrCl382AvnPT6V9X7gXsbh9OT1nRGOZSnwAxUQSrGKg5s6hidg9yVJwohz8g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CUFquwOKAEoQohW1PK+EBG6qtRkaTcfW/NthREQyNaPmWUhbFPMtp6HQQ77xOfbJ3U9iy2p9HA1EJ6MwuC+zLw==')})
  }
